\pard\widctlpar\sb100\sa100\kerning36\b\fs48 Understanding the challenge\par
\kerning0\b0\fs24 We highly recommend that you take a few dedicated minutes to read this README in its entirety before starting to think about potential solutions. You'll probably find it useful to review the examples and understand the problem at a high-level before digging into the specific details, many of which are covered in the FAQ.\par
\kerning36\b\fs48 Introduction\par
\kerning0\b0\fs24 Many investors, researchers, journalists and others use the Securities and Exchange Commission's Electronic Data Gathering, Analysis and Retrieval (EDGAR) system to retrieve financial documents, whether they are doing a deep dive into a particular company's financials or learning new information that a company has revealed through their filings.\par
The SEC maintains EDGAR weblogs showing which IP addresses have accessed which documents for what company, and at what day and time this occurred.\par
Imagine the SEC has asked you to take the data and produce a dashboard that would provide a real-time view into how users are accessing EDGAR, including how long they stay and the number of documents they access during the visit.\par
While the SEC usually makes its EDGAR weblogs publicly available after a six month delay, imagine that for this challenge, the government entity has promised it would stream the data into your program in real-time and with no delay.\par
Your job as a data engineer is to build a pipeline to ingest that stream of data and calculate how long a particular user spends on EDGAR during a visit and how many documents that user requests during the session.\par
\kerning36\b\fs48 Challenge summary\par
\kerning0\b0\fs24 For this challenge, we're asking you to take existing publicly available EDGAR weblogs and assume that each line represents a single web request for an EDGAR document that would be streamed into your program in real time.\par
Using the data, identify when a user visits, calculate the duration of and number of documents requested during that visit, and then write the output to a file.\par
Your role on the project is to work on the data pipeline to hand off the information to the front-end. As the backend data engineer, you do \b not\b0  need to display the data or work on the dashboard but you do need to provide the information.\par
You can assume there is another process that takes what is written to the output file and sends it to the front-end. If we were building this pipeline in real life, we\rquote d probably have another mechanism to send the output to the GUI rather than writing to a file. However, for the purposes of grading this challenge, we just want you to write the output to files.\par
\kerning36\b\fs48 Details of challenge\par
\kerning0\b0\fs24 For the purposes of this challenge, an IP address uniquely identifies a single user. A user is defined to have visited the EDGAR system if during the visit, the IP address requested one or more documents.\par
Also, for the purposes of this challenge, the amount of time that elapses between document requests should be used to determine when a visit, also referred to as a session, begins and ends.\par
A single user session is defined to have started when the IP address first requests a document from the EDGAR system and continues as long as the same user continues to make requests. The session is over after a certain period of time has elapsed -- we'll provide you that value -- and the user makes no requests for documents.\par
In other words, this period of inactivity helps to determine when the session is over and the user is assumed to have left the system.\par
The duration of any particular session is defined to be the time between the IP address' first request and the last one in the same session prior to the period of inactivity. If the user returns later to access another document requests, that subsequent request would be considered the start of a new session.\par
\kerning36\b\fs48 Implementation details\par
\kerning0\b0\fs24 Your program should expect two input files (be sure to read the section, "Repo directory structure", for details on where these files should be located):\par

\pard{\pntext\f5\'B7\tab}{\*\pn\pnlvlblt\pnf5\pnindent360{\pntxtb\'B7}}\widctlpar\fi-360\li720\sb100\sa100\f1\fs20 log.csv\f0\fs24 : EDGAR weblog data\par
{\pntext\f5\'B7\tab}\f1\fs20 inactivity_period.txt\f0\fs24 : Holds a single value denoting the period of inactivity that should be used to identify when a user session is over\par

\pard\widctlpar\sb100\sa100 As you process the EDGAR weblogs line by line, the moment you detect a user session has ended, your program should write a line to an output file, \f1\fs20 sessionization.txt\f0\fs24 , listing the IP address, duration of the session and number of documents accessed.\par
The value found in \f1\fs20 inactivity_period.txt\f0\fs24  should be used to determine when a session has ended and when a new session has possibly started. However, once you reach the end of the \f1\fs20 log.csv\f0\fs24 , that last timestamp should signal the end of all current sessions regardless of whether the period of inactivity has been met.\par
\b\fs36 Input files\par
\f1\fs20 log.csv\f0\fs27\par
\b0\fs24 The SEC provides weblogs stretching back years and is {{\field{\*\fldinst{HYPERLINK "https://www.sec.gov/dera/data/edgar-log-file-data-set.html" }}{\fldrslt{\ul\cf1\cf1\ul regularly updated, although with a six month delay}}}}\f0\fs24 .\par
For the purposes of this challenge, you can assume that the data is being streamed into your program in the same order that it appears in the file with the first line (after the header) being the first request and the last line being the latest. You also can assume the data is listed in chronological order for the purposes of this challenge.\par
While you're welcome to run your program using a subset of the data files found at the SEC's website, you should not assume that we'll be testing your program on any of those data files.\par
Also, while we won't expect your program to be able to process all of the SEC's weblogs (there is over 1TB of data), you should be prepared to talk about how you might design or redesign your program should the challenge be changed to require you to process hundreds of gigabytes or even a terabyte.\par
For the purposes of this challenge, below are the data fields you'll want to pay attention to from the SEC weblogs:\par

\pard{\pntext\f5\'B7\tab}{\*\pn\pnlvlblt\pnf5\pnindent360{\pntxtb\'B7}}\widctlpar\fi-360\li720\sb100\sa100\f1\fs20 ip\f0\fs24 : identifies the IP address of the device requesting the data. While the SEC anonymizes the last three digits, it uses a consistent formula that allows you to assume that any two \f1\fs20 ip\f0\fs24  fields with the duplicate values are referring to the same IP address\par
{\pntext\f5\'B7\tab}\f1\fs20 date\f0\fs24 : date of the request (yyyy-mm-dd)\par
{\pntext\f5\'B7\tab}\f1\fs20 time\f0\fs24 : time of the request (hh:mm:ss)\par
{\pntext\f5\'B7\tab}\f1\fs20 cik\f0\fs24 : SEC Central Index Key\par
{\pntext\f5\'B7\tab}\f1\fs20 accession\f0\fs24 : SEC document accession number\par
{\pntext\f5\'B7\tab}\f1\fs20 extention\f0\fs24 : Value that helps determine the document being requested\par

\pard\widctlpar\sb100\sa100 There are other fields that can be found in the weblogs. For the purposes of this challenge, your program can ignore those other fields.\par
Unlike other weblogs that contain the actual http web request, the SEC's files use a different but deterministic convention. For the purposes of this challenge, you can assume the combination of \f1\fs20 cik\f0\fs24 , \f1\fs20 accession\f0\fs24  and \f1\fs20 extention\f0\fs24  fields uniquely identifies a single web page document request. Don't assume any particular format for any of those three fields (e.g., the fields can consist of numbers, letters, hyphens, periods and other characters)\par
The first line of \f1\fs20 log.csv\f0\fs24  will be a header denoting the names of the fields in each web request. Each field is separated by a comma. Your program should only use this header to determine the order in which the fields will appear in the rest of the other lines in the same file.\par
\b\f1\fs20 inactivity_period.txt\f0\fs27\par
\b0\fs24 This file will hold a single integer value denoting the period of inactivity (in seconds) that your program should use to identify a user session. The value will range from 1 to 86,400 (i.e., one second to 24 hours)\par
\b\fs36 Output file\par
\b0\fs24 Once your program identifies the start and end of a session, it should gather the following fields and write them out to a line in the output file, \f1\fs20 sessionization.txt\f0\fs24 . The fields on each line must be separated by a \f1\fs20 ,\f0\fs24 :\par

\pard{\pntext\f5\'B7\tab}{\*\pn\pnlvlblt\pnf5\pnindent360{\pntxtb\'B7}}\widctlpar\fi-360\li720\sb100\sa100 IP address of the user exactly as found in \f1\fs20 log.csv\f0\fs24\par
{\pntext\f5\'B7\tab}date and time of the first webpage request in the session (yyyy-mm-dd hh:mm:ss)\par
{\pntext\f5\'B7\tab}date and time of the last webpage request in the session (yyyy-mm-dd hh:mm:ss)\par
{\pntext\f5\'B7\tab}duration of the session in seconds\par
{\pntext\f5\'B7\tab}count of webpage requests during the session\par

\pard\widctlpar\sb100\sa100 Unlike the input weblog data file and for the purposes of this challenge, your program should not write a header line to the output file but instead write just the results. Each line should have the fields in the exact order detailed above. Fields must be separated by a comma.\par
If your program is able to detect multiple user sessions ending at the same time, it should write the results to the \f1\fs20 sessionization.txt\f0\fs24  output file in the same order as the user's first request for that session appeared in the input \f1\fs20 log.csv\f0\fs24  file.\par
\kerning36\b\fs48 Example\par
\kerning0\b0\fs24 Suppose your input files contained only the following few lines. Note that the fields we are interested in are in \b bold\b0  below but will not be like that in the input file. There's also an extra newline between records below, but the input file won't have that.\par
\b\f1\fs20 inactivity_period.txt\b0\f0\fs24\par

\pard\widctlpar\sa100\b 2\b0\par

\pard\widctlpar\sb100\sa100\b\f1\fs20 log.csv\b0\f0\fs24\par

\pard\widctlpar\sa100\b ip,date,time\b0 ,zone,\b cik,accession,extention\b0 ,code,size,idx,norefer,noagent,find,crawler,browser\par
\b 101.81.133.jja,2017-06-30,00:00:00\b0 ,0.0,\b 1608552.0,0001047469-17-004337,-index.htm\b0 ,200.0,80251.0,1.0,0.0,0.0,9.0,0.0,\par
\b 107.23.85.jfd,2017-06-30,00:00:00\b0 ,0.0,\b 1027281.0,0000898430-02-001167,-index.htm\b0 ,200.0,2825.0,1.0,0.0,0.0,10.0,0.0,\par
\b 107.23.85.jfd,2017-06-30,00:00:00\b0 ,0.0,\b 1136894.0,0000905148-07-003827,-index.htm\b0 ,200.0,3021.0,1.0,0.0,0.0,10.0,0.0,\par
\b 107.23.85.jfd,2017-06-30,00:00:01\b0 ,0.0,\b 841535.0,0000841535-98-000002,-index.html\b0 ,200.0,2699.0,1.0,0.0,0.0,10.0,0.0,\par
\b 108.91.91.hbc,2017-06-30,00:00:01\b0 ,0.0,\b 1295391.0,0001209784-17-000052,.txt\b0 ,200.0,19884.0,0.0,0.0,0.0,10.0,0.0,\par

\b 108.91.91.hbc,2017-06-30,00:00:04\b0 ,0.0,\b 1618174.0,0001140361-17-026711,.txt\b0 ,301.0,674.0,0.0,0.0,0.0,10.0,0.0,\par

\pard\widctlpar\sb100\sa100 The single line on \f1\fs20 inactivity_period.txt\f0\fs24  tells us that once two seconds have elapsed since a user made a document request, we can assume that user's particular visit has ended. Any subsequent requests would be considered a new session.\par
The first day and time listed in the input file is 2017-06-30 and the time is 00:00:00. That means at that date and time, the following ip addresses initiated a visit to EDGAR:\par

\pard{\pntext\f5\'B7\tab}{\*\pn\pnlvlblt\pnf5\pnindent360{\pntxtb\'B7}}\widctlpar\fi-360\li720\sb100\sa100\b 101.81.133.jja\b0  made a request for cik: \b 1608552.0\b0 , accession: \b 0001047469-17-004337\b0  and extention: \b -index.htm\b0\par
{\pntext\f5\'B7\tab}\b 107.23.85.jfd\b0  made a request for cik: \b 1027281.0\b0 , accession: \b 0000898430-02-001167\b0  and extention: \b -index.htm\b0\par
{\pntext\f5\'B7\tab}\b 107.23.85.jfd\b0  made a request for cik: \b 1136894.0\b0 , accession: \b 0000905148-07-003827\b0  and extention: \b -index.htm\b0\par

\pard\widctlpar\sb100\sa100 So for the first second of data that your program has encountered, it knows one user has accessed one document and a second user has requested two:\par

At that point, it should write the results to the output file, and the entire content of \f1\fs20 sessionization.txt\f0\fs24  should be:\par

\pard\widctlpar\tx916\tx1832\tx2748\tx3664\tx4580\tx5496\tx6412\tx7328\tx8244\tx9160\tx10076\tx10992\tx11908\tx12824\tx13740\tx14656\f1\fs20 101.81.133.jja,2017-06-30 00:00:00,2017-06-30 00:00:00,1,1\par
108.91.91.hbc,2017-06-30 00:00:01,2017-06-30 00:00:01,1,1\par
107.23.85.jfd,2017-06-30 00:00:00,2017-06-30 00:00:03,4,4\par
106.120.173.jie,2017-06-30 00:00:02,2017-06-30 00:00:02,1,1\par
107.178.195.aag,2017-06-30 00:00:02,2017-06-30 00:00:04,3,2\par
108.91.91.hbc,2017-06-30 00:00:04,2017-06-30 00:00:04,1,1\par

\pard\widctlpar\sb100\sa100\f0\fs24 Notice from the above output that the first two lines were the ones we had already written.\par
The third line details the session for \f1\fs20 107.23.85.jfd\f0\fs24  next because its first document request came at \f1\fs20 2017-06-30 00:00:00\f0\fs24 , which is earlier than any of the other remaining sessions.\par
The fourth line belongs to IP address, \f1\fs20 106.120.173.jie\f0\fs24  because that user's first document request came at \f1\fs20 2017-06-30 00:00:02\f0\fs24 . The first document request from \f1\fs20 107.178.195.aag\f0\fs24  also comes at the same time but it is listed after \f1\fs20 106.120.173.jie\f0\fs24  in the input file so that is why it is listed on the fifth line.\par
The second session detected for \f1\fs20 108.91.91.hbc\f0\fs24  concludes the \f1\fs20 sessionization.txt\f0\fs24  file.\par
\b\fs36 Writing clean, scalable and well-tested code\par
\b0\fs24 As a data engineer, it\rquote s important that you write clean, well-documented code that scales for large amounts of data. For this reason, it\rquote s important to ensure that your solution works well for a large number of records, rather than just the above example.\par
It's also important to use software engineering best practices like unit tests, especially since data is not always clean and predictable. For more details about the implementation, please refer to the FAQ below. If further clarification is necessary, email us at {{\field{\*\fldinst{HYPERLINK "mailto:cc@insightdataengineering.com" }}{\fldrslt{\ul\cf1\cf1\ul cc@insightdataengineering.com}}}}\f0\fs24  but please do so only after you have read through the Readme and FAQ one more time and cannot find the answer to your question.\par
Before submitting your solution you should summarize your approach, dependencies and run instructions (if any) in your \f1\fs20 README\f0\fs24 .\par
You may write your solution in any mainstream programming language such as C, C++, C#, Clojure, Erlang, Go, Haskell, Java, Python, Ruby, or Scala. Once completed, submit a link to a Github repo with your source code.\par
In addition to the source code, the top-most directory of your repo must include the \f1\fs20 input\f0\fs24  and \f1\fs20 output\f0\fs24  directories, and a shell script named \f1\fs20 run.sh\f0\fs24  that compiles and runs the program(s) that implement the required features.\par
If your solution requires additional libraries, environments, or dependencies, you must specify these in your \f1\fs20 README\f0\fs24  documentation. See the figure below for the required structure of the top-most directory in your repo, or simply clone this repo.\par
\b\fs36 Repo directory structure\par
\b0\fs24 The directory structure for your repo should look like this:\par

\pard\widctlpar\tx916\tx1832\tx2748\tx3664\tx4580\tx5496\tx6412\tx7328\tx8244\tx9160\tx10076\tx10992\tx11908\tx12824\tx13740\tx14656\f4\fs20\u9500?\u9472?\u9472?\f1  README.md \par
\f4\u9500?\u9472?\u9472?\f1  run.sh\par
\f4\u9500?\u9472?\u9472?\f1  src\par
\f4\u9474?\f1    \f4\u9492?\u9472?\u9472?\f1  sessionization.py\par
\f4\u9500?\u9472?\u9472?\f1  input\par
\f4\u9474?\f1    \f4\u9492?\u9472?\u9472?\f1  inactivity_period.txt\par
\f4\u9474?\f1    \f4\u9492?\u9472?\u9472?\f1  log.csv\par
\f4\u9500?\u9472?\u9472?\f1  output\par
|   \f4\u9492?\u9472?\u9472?\f1  sessionization.txt\par
\f4\u9500?\u9472?\u9472?\f1  insight_testsuite\par
    \f4\u9492?\u9472?\u9472?\f1  run_tests.sh\par
    \f4\u9492?\u9472?\u9472?\f1  tests\par
        \f4\u9492?\u9472?\u9472?\f1  test_1\par
        |   \f4\u9500?\u9472?\u9472?\f1  input\par
        |   \f4\u9474?\f1    \f4\u9492?\u9472?\u9472?\f1  inactivity_period.txt\par
        |   \f4\u9474?\f1    \f4\u9492?\u9472?\u9472?\f1  log.csv\par
        |   |__ output\par
        |   \f4\u9474?\f1    \f4\u9492?\u9472?\u9472?\f1  sessionization.txt\par
        \f4\u9500?\u9472?\u9472?\f1  your-own-test_1\par
            \f4\u9500?\u9472?\u9472?\f1  input\par
            \f4\u9474?\f1    \f4\u9492?\u9472?\u9472?\f1  your-own-inputs\par
            |\f4\u9472?\u9472?\f1  output\par
                \f4\u9492?\u9472?\u9472?\f1  sessionization.txt\par

\pard\widctlpar\sb100\sa100\b\f0\fs24 Don't fork this repo\b0  and don't use this \f1\fs20 README\f0\fs24  instead of your own. The content of \f1\fs20 src\f0\fs24  does not need to be a single file called \f1\fs20 sessionization.py\f0\fs24 , which is only an example. Instead, you should include your own source files and give them expressive names.\par
\b\fs36 Testing your directory structure and output format\par
\b0\fs24 To make sure that your code has the correct directory structure and the format of the output files are correct, we have included a test script called \f1\fs20 run_tests.sh\f0\fs24  in the \f1\fs20 insight_testsuite\f0\fs24  folder.\par
The tests are stored simply as text files under the \f1\fs20 insight_testsuite/tests\f0\fs24  folder. Each test should have a separate folder with an \f1\fs20 input\f0\fs24  folder for \f1\fs20 inactivity_period.txt\f0\fs24  and \f1\fs20 log.csv\f0\fs24  and an \f1\fs20 output\f0\fs24  folder for \f1\fs20 sessionization.txt\f0\fs24 .\par
You can run the test with the following command from within the \f1\fs20 insight_testsuite\f0\fs24  folder:\par

\pard\widctlpar\tx916\tx1832\tx2748\tx3664\tx4580\tx5496\tx6412\tx7328\tx8244\tx9160\tx10076\tx10992\tx11908\tx12824\tx13740\tx14656\f1\fs20 insight_testsuite~$ ./run_tests.sh \par

\pard\widctlpar\sb100\sa100\f0\fs24 On a failed test, the output of \f1\fs20 run_tests.sh\f0\fs24  should look like:\par

\pard\widctlpar\tx916\tx1832\tx2748\tx3664\tx4580\tx5496\tx6412\tx7328\tx8244\tx9160\tx10076\tx10992\tx11908\tx12824\tx13740\tx14656\f1\fs20 [FAIL]: test_1\par
[Thu Mar 30 16:28:01 PDT 2017] 0 of 1 tests passed\par

\pard\widctlpar\sb100\sa100\f0\fs24 On success:\par

\pard\widctlpar\tx916\tx1832\tx2748\tx3664\tx4580\tx5496\tx6412\tx7328\tx8244\tx9160\tx10076\tx10992\tx11908\tx12824\tx13740\tx14656\f1\fs20 [PASS]: test_1\par
[Thu Mar 30 16:25:57 PDT 2017] 1 of 1 tests passed\par

\pard\widctlpar\sb100\sa100\f0\fs24 One test has been provided as a way to check your formatting and simulate how we will be running tests when you submit your solution. We urge you to write your own additional tests. \f1\fs20 test_1\f0\fs24  is only intended to alert you if the directory structure or the output for this test is incorrect.\par
Your submission must pass at least the provided test in order to pass the coding challenge.\par
\b\fs36 Instructions to submit your solution\par

\pard{\pntext\f5\'B7\tab}{\*\pn\pnlvlblt\pnf5\pnindent360{\pntxtb\'B7}}\widctlpar\fi-360\li720\sb100\sa100\b0\fs24 To submit your entry please use the link you received in your coding challenge invite email\par
{\pntext\f5\'B7\tab}You will only be able to submit through the link one time\par
{\pntext\f5\'B7\tab}Do NOT attach a file - we will not admit solutions which are attached files\par
{\pntext\f5\'B7\tab}Use the submission box to enter the link to your GitHub repo or Bitbucket ONLY\par
{\pntext\f5\'B7\tab}Link to the specific repo for this project, not your general profile\par
{\pntext\f5\'B7\tab}Put any comments in the README inside your project repo, not in the submission box\par
{\pntext\f5\'B7\tab}We are unable to accept coding challenges that are emailed to us\par
